srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Philadelphia_%285559907949%29.png/330px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Philadelphia_%285559907949%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Philadelphia_%285559907949%29.png/440px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Philadelphia_%285559907949%29.png 2x" data-file-width="3009" data-file-height="3009" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Philadelphia_(5559907949).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of racial distribution in Philadelphia, 2010 Census. Each dot is 25 people: <span style="color:#ff0000"><b>White</b></span>, <span style="color:#0000ff"><b>Black</b></span>, <span style="color:#00ff80"><b>Asian</b></span>, <span style="color:#ff8000"><b>Hispanic</b></span>, or <span style="color:#cccc00"><b>Other</b></span>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a> redistricting data indicated that the racial makeup of the city was 644,287 (42.2%) <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">Black</a> (non-Hispanic), 562,585 (36.9%) <a href="/wiki/White_Americans" title="White Americans">White</a> (non-Hispanic), 96,405 (6.3%) <a href="/wiki/Asian_Americans" title="Asian Americans">Asian</a> (2.0% <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans" title="Chinese Americans">Chinese</a>, 1.2% <a href="/wiki/Indian_Americans" title="Indian Americans">Indian</a>, 0.9% <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Americans" title="Vietnamese Americans">Vietnamese</a>, 0.4% <a href="/wiki/Korean_Americans" title="Korean Americans">Korean</a>, 0.3% <a href="/wiki/Filipino_Americans" title="Filipino Americans">Filipino</a>, 0.1% <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Americans" title="Japanese Americans">Japanese</a>, and 1.4% other), 6,996 (0.5%) <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans</a>, 744 (0.05%) <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Americans" title="Pacific Islands Americans">Pacific Islanders</a>, and 43,070 (2.8%) from two or more races. <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race were 187,611 persons (12.3%); 8.0% of Philadelphia is <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans_in_the_United_States" title="Puerto Ricans in the United States">Puerto Rican</a>, 1.0% <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Americans" title="Mexican Americans">Mexican</a>, 0.3% <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Americans" title="Cuban Americans">Cuban</a>, and 3.0% other. The racial breakdown of Philadelphia\'s Hispanic/Latino population was 63,636 (33.9%) White, 17,552 (9.4%) Black, 3,498 (1.9%) Native American, 884 (0.47%) Asian, 287 (0.15%) Pacific Islander, 86,626 (46.2%) from other races, and 15,128 (8.1%) from two or more races.<sup id="cite_ref-Gen_Pop/Housing_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gen_Pop/Housing-105">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The five largest European ancestries reported in the 2010 Census included <a href="/wiki/Irish_Americans" title="Irish Americans">Irish</a> (13.0%), <a href="/wiki/Italian_Americans" title="Italian Americans">Italian</a> (8.3%), <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">German</a> (8.2%), <a href="/wiki/Polish_Americans" title="Polish Americans">Polish</a> (3.9%), and <a href="/wiki/English_Americans" title="English Americans">English</a> (3.1%).<sup id="cite_ref-2010_Ancestry_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Ancestry-109">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The estimated average population density was 11,782 people per square&#160;mile (4,549/km\xc2\xb2) in 2017. In 2010, the Census Bureau reported that 1,468,623 people (96.2% of the population) lived in households, 38,007 (2.5%) lived in non-institutionalized group quarters, and 19,376 (1.3%) were institutionalized.<sup id="cite_ref-Gen_Pop/Housing_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gen_Pop/Housing-105">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the city reported having 668,247 total housing units, down slightly from 670,171 housing units in 2010. As of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 87 percent of housing units were occupied, while 13 percent were vacant, a slight change from 2010 where 89.5 percent of units were occupied, or 599,736 and 10.5 percent were vacant, or 70,435.<sup id="cite_ref-Gen_Pop/Housing_105-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gen_Pop/Housing-105">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Of the city\'s residents, 32 percent reported having no vehicles available while 23 percent had two or more vehicles available, as of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, 24.9 percent of households reported having children under the age of 18 living with them, 28.3 percent were married couples living together and 22.5 percent had a female householder with no husband present, 6.0 percent had a male householder with no wife present, and 43.2 percent were non-families. The city reported 34.1 percent of all households were made up of individuals while 10.5 percent had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.45 and the average family size was 3.20.<sup id="cite_ref-Gen_Pop/Housing_105-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gen_Pop/Housing-105">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the percentage of women who gave birth in the previous 12 months who were unmarried was 56 percent. Of Philadelphia\'s adults, 31 percent were married or lived as a couple, 55 percent were not married, 11 percent were divorced or separated, and 3 percent were widowed.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the Census Bureau, the median household income in 2013 was $36,836, down 7.9 percent from 2008 when the <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a>-adjusted median household income was $40,008 (in 2013 dollars). For comparison, on an inflation-adjusted basis, the median household income among metropolitan areas was $60,482, down 8.2 percent in the same period, and the national median household income was $55,250, down 7.0 percent from 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s wealth disparity is evident when neighborhoods are compared. Residents in <a href="/wiki/Society_Hill" title="Society Hill">Society Hill</a> had a 2013 median household income of $93,720, while residents in one of <a href="/wiki/North_Philadelphia" title="North Philadelphia">North Philadelphia</a>\'s districts reported the lowest median household income, $14,185.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the last decade, Philadelphia experienced a large shift in its age profile. In 2000, the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">population pyramid</a> had a largely stationary shape. In 2013, the city took on an expansive pyramid shape, with an increase in the three <a href="/wiki/Millennials" title="Millennials">millennial</a> age groups, 20 to 24, 25 to 29, and 30 to 34. The city\'s 25- to 29-year-old age group was the city\'s largest age cohort.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> According to the 2010 Census, 343,837 (22.5%) were under the age of 18; 203,697 (13.3%) from 18 to 24; 434,385 (28.5%) from 25 to 44; 358,778 (23.5%) from 45 to 64; and 185,309 (12.1%) who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 33.5 years. For every 100 females, there were 89.4 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 85.7 males.<sup id="cite_ref-Gen_Pop/Housing_105-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gen_Pop/Housing-105">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The city had 22,018 births in 2013, down from a peak 23,689 births in 2008. Philadelphia\'s death rate was at its lowest in at least a half-century, 13,691 deaths in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Another factor attributing to the population increase is Philadelphia\'s rising <a href="/wiki/Immigration_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigration rate">immigration rate</a>. Like the millennial population, Philadelphia\'s <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigrant</a> population is also growing rapidly; according to a study by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Charitable_Trusts" class="mw-redirect" title="Pew Charitable Trusts">Pew Charitable Trusts</a>, the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Foreign_born" title="Foreign born">foreign-born</a> population had increased by 69% between 2000 and 2016 to constitute nearly 20% of Philadelpia\'s work force.<sup id="cite_ref-PhiladelphiaImmigrants_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhiladelphiaImmigrants-111">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Irish_Memorial_in_Philadelphia_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Irish_Memorial_in_Philadelphia_1.jpg/220px-Irish_Memorial_in_Philadelphia_1.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Irish_Memorial_in_Philadelphia_1.jpg/330px-Irish_Memorial_in_Philadelphia_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Irish_Memorial_in_Philadelphia_1.jpg/440px-Irish_Memorial_in_Philadelphia_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2248" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Irish_Memorial_in_Philadelphia_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Leacht Quimhneachain Na Gael", an <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">Irish famine</a> memorial at <a href="/wiki/Penn%27s_Landing" title="Penn&#39;s Landing">Penn\'s Landing</a> honors the large <a href="/wiki/Irish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish American">Irish</a> community (14.2% of the city\'s population).<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Irish, Italian, German, Polish, English, Russian, Ukrainian and French are the largest ethnic European groups in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-2010_Ancestry_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Ancestry-109">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia has the second-largest Irish and Italian populations in the United States, after New York City. <a href="/wiki/South_Philadelphia" title="South Philadelphia">South Philadelphia</a> remains one of the largest Italian neighborhoods in the country and is home to the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Market,_Philadelphia" title="Italian Market, Philadelphia">Italian Market</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Pennsport,_Philadelphia" title="Pennsport, Philadelphia">Pennsport</a> neighborhood and <a href="/wiki/Grays_Ferry,_Philadelphia" title="Grays Ferry, Philadelphia">Gray\'s Ferry</a> section of South Philadelphia, home to many <a href="/wiki/Mummers_Parade" title="Mummers Parade">Mummer</a> clubs, are well known as Irish neighborhoods. The <a href="/wiki/Kensington,_Philadelphia" title="Kensington, Philadelphia">Kensington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Richmond,_Philadelphia" title="Port Richmond, Philadelphia">Port Richmond</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fishtown,_Philadelphia" title="Fishtown, Philadelphia">Fishtown</a> neighborhoods have historically been heavily Irish and Polish. Port Richmond is well known in particular as the center of the Polish immigrant and Polish-American community in Philadelphia, and it remains a common destination for Polish immigrants. <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Philadelphia" title="Northeast Philadelphia">Northeast Philadelphia</a>, although known for its Irish and Irish-American population, is also home to a large Jewish and Russian population. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Airy,_Philadelphia" title="Mount Airy, Philadelphia">Mount Airy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Philadelphia" title="Northwest Philadelphia">Northwest Philadelphia</a> also contains a large Jewish community, while nearby <a href="/wiki/Chestnut_Hill,_Philadelphia" title="Chestnut Hill, Philadelphia">Chestnut Hill</a> is historically known as an <a href="/wiki/White_Anglo-Saxon_Protestant" title="White Anglo-Saxon Protestant">Anglo-Saxon Protestant</a> community.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:13th_Gayborhood.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/13th_Gayborhood.jpg/180px-13th_Gayborhood.jpg" width="180" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/13th_Gayborhood.jpg/270px-13th_Gayborhood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/13th_Gayborhood.jpg/360px-13th_Gayborhood.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1712" data-file-height="2288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:13th_Gayborhood.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/LGBT_culture_in_Philadelphia" title="LGBT culture in Philadelphia">Gayborhood</a> <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_flag_(LGBT_movement)" title="Rainbow flag (LGBT movement)">street sign</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_West,_Philadelphia" title="Washington Square West, Philadelphia">Washington Square</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Philadelphia is also home to a significant <a href="/wiki/Gay" title="Gay">gay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesbian" title="Lesbian">lesbian</a> population. Philadelphia\'s <a href="/wiki/Gay_village" title="Gay village">Gayborhood</a>, which is located near <a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_(Philadelphia)" title="Washington Square (Philadelphia)">Washington Square</a>, is home to a large concentration of gay and lesbian friendly businesses, restaurants, and bars.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">Black American</a> population in Philadelphia is the third-largest in the country, after New York City and Chicago. Historically, <a href="/wiki/West_Philadelphia" title="West Philadelphia">West Philadelphia</a> and North Philadelphia were largely black neighborhoods, but many are leaving those areas in favor of the Northeast and Southwest sections of Philadelphia. There is a higher proportion of Muslims in the Black American population than most cities in America. West Philadelphia also has significant Caribbean and African immigrant populations.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans_in_Philadelphia" title="Puerto Ricans in Philadelphia">Puerto Rican</a> population in Philadelphia is the second-largest after New York City, and the second-fastest growing after Orlando.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> There are large Puerto Rican and <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Americans" title="Dominican Americans">Dominican</a> populations in <a href="/wiki/North_Philadelphia" title="North Philadelphia">North Philadelphia</a> and the Northeast, as well as a significant Mexican population in South Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia\'s <a href="/wiki/Asian_Americans" title="Asian Americans">Asian American</a> population originated mainly from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. Over 35,000 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans" title="Chinese Americans">Chinese Americans</a> made their home within Philadelphia city proper alone in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> including a large <a href="/wiki/Fuzhounese_Americans" title="Fuzhounese Americans">Fuzhounese</a> population, and the city hosts a growing <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Philadelphia" title="Chinatown, Philadelphia">Chinatown</a> accommodating heavily traveled <a href="/wiki/Chinatown_bus_lines" title="Chinatown bus lines">Chinese-owned bus lines</a> to and from <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">Chinatown, Manhattan</a> in New York City. While a large Korean community initially settled in the North Philadelphia neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Olney,_Philadelphia" title="Olney, Philadelphia">Olney</a>, the primary <a href="/wiki/Koreatown,_Philadelphia" title="Koreatown, Philadelphia">Koreatown</a> has subsequently evolved in North Philadelphia straddling the border with the northern suburb of <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham,_Pennsylvania" title="Cheltenham, Pennsylvania">Cheltenham</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Montgomery County, Pennsylvania">Montgomery County</a>. South Philadelphia is also home to large <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_Americans" title="Cambodian Americans">Cambodian</a>, Vietnamese, and Chinese communities. Philadelphia has the fifth largest <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> population among American cities.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_the_Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Interior_of_the_Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul.JPG/220px-Interior_of_the_Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Interior_of_the_Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul.JPG/330px-Interior_of_the_Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Interior_of_the_Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul.JPG/440px-Interior_of_the_Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_the_Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul_(Philadelphia)" title="Cathedral Basilica of Saints Peter and Paul (Philadelphia)">Cathedral Basilica of Saints Peter and Paul</a></div></div></div>\n<p>According to a 2014 study by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 68% of the population of the city identified themselves as <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a>, with 41% professing attendance at a variety of churches that could be considered <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a>, 26% professing <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> beliefs, and less than 1% are <a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">Mormons</a>, while the remaining 24% claim <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religious affiliation</a>. The same study says that other religions collectively compose about 8% of the population, including <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Philadelphia <a href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">metropolitan area</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Philadelphia" title="History of the Jews in Philadelphia">Jewish</a> population was estimated at 206,000 in 2001, which was the sixth largest in the United States at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other religious groups in Philadelphia include <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Philadelphia" title="Chinatown, Philadelphia">Chinatown</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religions" title="Traditional African religions">traditional African religions</a> in North and West Philadelphia. Historically, the city has strong connections to the <a href="/wiki/Quakers" title="Quakers">Quakers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Universalism" title="Unitarian Universalism">Unitarian Universalism</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ethical_movement" title="Ethical movement">Ethical Culture movement</a>, all of which continue to be represented in the city. The Quaker <a href="/wiki/Friends_General_Conference" title="Friends General Conference">Friends General Conference</a> is based in Philadelphia.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Afro-American_religion" title="Afro-American religion">African diasporic religions</a> are practiced in some Hispanic and Caribbean communities in North and West Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Italian_Market_Vegetable_Stand_3000px.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Italian_Market_Vegetable_Stand_3000px.jpg/220px-Italian_Market_Vegetable_Stand_3000px.jpg" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Italian_Market_Vegetable_Stand_3000px.jpg/330px-Italian_Market_Vegetable_Stand_3000px.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Italian_Market_Vegetable_Stand_3000px.jpg/440px-Italian_Market_Vegetable_Stand_3000px.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Italian_Market_Vegetable_Stand_3000px.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Italian_Market,_Philadelphia" title="Italian Market, Philadelphia">Italian Market</a>, part of <a href="/wiki/South_Philadelphia" title="South Philadelphia">South Philadelphia</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Italian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian American">Italian</a> heritage<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>As of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 79.12% (1,112,441) of Philadelphia residents age 5 and older spoke <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> at home as a <a href="/wiki/Primary_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary language">primary language</a>, while 9.72% (136,688) spoke <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, 1.64% (23,075) <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, 0.89% (12,499) <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>, 0.77% (10,885) <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, 0.66% (9,240) <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, 0.61% (8,639) <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Asia" title="Languages of Asia">other Asian languages</a>, 0.58% (8,217) <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">African languages</a>, 0.56% (7,933) <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambodian language">Cambodian</a> (<a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Mon-Khmer</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> was spoken as a <a href="/wiki/Main_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Main language">main language</a> by 0.55% (7,773) of the population over the age of five. In total, 20.88% (293,544) of Philadelphia\'s population age 5 and older spoke a <a href="/wiki/Mother_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother language">mother language</a> other than English.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialect">Dialect</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_English" title="Philadelphia English">Philadelphia English</a></div>\n<p>The traditional Philadelphia accent is considered by some <a href="/wiki/Linguist" class="mw-redirect" title="Linguist">linguists</a> to be the most distinctive accent in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-Fades_Out_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fades_Out-127">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The Philadelphia dialect, which is spread throughout the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Valley" title="Delaware Valley">Delaware Valley</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Jersey" title="South Jersey">South Jersey</a>, is part of a larger <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_American_English" title="Mid-Atlantic American English">Mid-Atlantic American English</a> family, a designation that also includes the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltimore dialect">Baltimore dialect</a>. Additionally, it shares many similarities with the <a href="/wiki/New_York_accent" title="New York accent">New York accent</a>.\n</p><p>Thanks to over a century of linguistic data collected by researchers at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a> under sociolinguist <a href="/wiki/William_Labov" title="William Labov">William Labov</a>, the Philadelphia dialect has been one of the best-studied forms of <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Avril_2012_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avril_2012-129">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup> The accent is especially found within the <a href="/wiki/Irish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish American">Irish American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian American">Italian American</a> <a href="/wiki/Working-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Working-class">working-class</a> neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia also has its own unique collection of <a href="/wiki/Neologism" title="Neologism">neologisms</a> and slang terms.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Philadelphia" title="Economy of Philadelphia">Economy of Philadelphia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_the_Philadelphia_area" title="List of companies based in the Philadelphia area">List of companies based in the Philadelphia area</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable floatright" style="font-size:90%; text-align:center;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td colspan="3" style="background:#9BDDFF;"><b>Top publicly traded companies<br />headquartered in Philadelphia</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<td><b>Corporation</b></td>\n<td><b>Rank</b></td>\n<td><b>Revenue</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a></td>\n<td>31</td>\n<td>80.4\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Aramark" title="Aramark">Aramark</a></td>\n<td>192</td>\n<td>14.4\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Crown_Holdings" title="Crown Holdings">Crown Holdings</a></td>\n<td>333</td>\n<td>8.3\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Urban_Outfitters" title="Urban Outfitters">Urban Outfitters</a></td>\n<td>645</td>\n<td>3.5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/FMC_Corporation" title="FMC Corporation">FMC</a></td>\n<td>681</td>\n<td>3.3\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="6"><i>Revenue in billions for <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">FY</a> 2016</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="6"><b>Source:</b> <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Philadelphia is the center of economic activity in <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> with the headquarters of five <a href="/wiki/Fortune_1000" title="Fortune 1000">Fortune 1000</a> companies located within city limits. According to the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">Bureau of Economic Analysis</a>, the Philadelphia area had a total <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> of $431&#160;billion in 2016, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._metropolitan_areas_by_GDP" title="List of U.S. metropolitan areas by GDP">eighth-largest metropolitan economy</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Gross_Metropolitan_Product_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gross_Metropolitan_Product-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia was rated by the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">GaWC</a> as a \'Beta\' city in its 2016 ranking of <a href="/wiki/Global_city#GaWC_study" title="Global city">world cities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Airport" title="Philadelphia International Airport">Philadelphia International Airport</a> is undergoing a $900&#160;million infrastructural expansion to increase passenger capacity and augment passenger experience;<sup id="cite_ref-PhiladelphiaAirportExpansion1_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhiladelphiaAirportExpansion1-135">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PhiladelphiaAirportExpansion2_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhiladelphiaAirportExpansion2-136">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Philadelphia" title="Port of Philadelphia">Port of Philadelphia</a>, having experienced the highest percentage growth by <a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">tonnage</a> loaded in 2017 among major U.S. seaports, was in the process of doubling its capacity in order to accommodate super-sized <a href="/wiki/Post-Panamax" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-Panamax">post-Panamax</a> shipping vessels in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-PhiladelphiaSeaportExpnasion1_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhiladelphiaSeaportExpnasion1-137">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia\'s economic sectors include <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>. Financial activities account for the largest economic sector of the metropolitan area, which is also one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Health_education" title="Health education">health education</a> and research centers in the United States.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WTP_D05_AMP_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/WTP_D05_AMP_2.jpg/220px-WTP_D05_AMP_2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/WTP_D05_AMP_2.jpg/330px-WTP_D05_AMP_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/WTP_D05_AMP_2.jpg/440px-WTP_D05_AMP_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WTP_D05_AMP_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Stock_Exchange" title="Philadelphia Stock Exchange">Philadelphia Stock Exchange</a>, the oldest <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> in the United States</div></div></div>\n<p>The city is home to the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Stock_Exchange" title="Philadelphia Stock Exchange">Philadelphia Stock Exchange</a> and some of the area\'s largest companies including cable television and internet provider <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a>, insurance companies <a href="/wiki/Cigna" title="Cigna">Cigna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Penn" title="Colonial Penn">Colonial Penn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Independence_Blue_Cross" title="Independence Blue Cross">Independence Blue Cross</a>, energy company <a href="/wiki/Sunoco" title="Sunoco">Sunoco</a>, food services company <a href="/wiki/Aramark" title="Aramark">Aramark</a>, packaging company <a href="/wiki/Crown_Holdings" title="Crown Holdings">Crown Holdings</a>, chemical makers <a href="/wiki/FMC_Corporation" title="FMC Corporation">FMC</a> and  <a href="/wiki/Rohm_and_Haas" title="Rohm and Haas">Rohm and Haas</a>, pharmaceutical company <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Rotorcraft_Systems" title="Boeing Rotorcraft Systems">Boeing Rotorcraft Systems</a>, apparel retailer <a href="/wiki/Urban_Outfitters" title="Urban Outfitters">Urban Outfitters</a>, and automotive parts retailer <a href="/wiki/Pep_Boys" title="Pep Boys">Pep Boys</a>.\n</p><p>Philadelphia\'s annualized unemployment rate was 7.8% in 2014, down from 10% the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> This is higher than the national average of 6.2%. Similarly, the rate of new jobs added to the city\'s economy lagged behind the national job growth. In 2014, about 8,800 jobs were added to the city\'s economy. Sectors with the largest number of jobs added were in education and health care, <a href="/wiki/Leisure" title="Leisure">leisure</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hospitality" title="Hospitality">hospitality</a>, and professional and business services. Declines were seen in the city\'s manufacturing and government sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>About 31.9% of the city\'s population was not in the labor force in 2015, the second highest percentage after <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>. The city\'s two largest employers are the federal and city governments. Philadelphia\'s largest private employer is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a> followed by the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Hospital_of_Philadelphia" title="Children&#39;s Hospital of Philadelphia">Children\'s Hospital of Philadelphia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> A study commissioned by the city\'s government in 2011 projected 40,000 jobs would be added to the city within 25 years, raising the number of jobs from 675,000 in 2010 to an estimated 715,000 by 2035.<sup id="cite_ref-Philadelphia2035_Summary_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philadelphia2035_Summary-138">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia\'s history attracts many tourists, with the <a href="/wiki/Independence_National_Historical_Park" title="Independence National Historical Park">Independence National Historical Park</a> (which includes the <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Bell" title="Liberty Bell">Liberty Bell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Independence_Hall" title="Independence Hall">Independence Hall</a>, and other historic sites) receiving over 5 million visitors in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The city welcomed 42 million domestic tourists in 2016 who spent $6.8 billion, generating an estimated $11 billion in total economic impact in the city and surrounding four counties of Pennsylvania.<sup id="cite_ref-Visit_Philadelphia_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visit_Philadelphia-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Philadelphia" title="Education in Philadelphia">Education in Philadelphia</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">Primary and secondary education</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Penn_Charter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f8/Penn_Charter.jpg/220px-Penn_Charter.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f8/Penn_Charter.jpg/330px-Penn_Charter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f8/Penn_Charter.jpg/440px-Penn_Charter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="802" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Penn_Charter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Penn_Charter_School" title="William Penn Charter School">William Penn Charter School</a>, established in 1689, is the oldest <a href="/wiki/Quaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaker">Quaker</a> school in the nation</div></div></div>\n<p>Education in Philadelphia is provided by many private and public institutions. The <a href="/wiki/School_District_of_Philadelphia" title="School District of Philadelphia">School District of Philadelphia</a> runs the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Public_school_(government_funded)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public school (government funded)">public schools</a>. The Philadelphia School District is the eighth largest <a href="/wiki/School_district" title="School district">school district</a> in the United States<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> with 142,266 students in 218 traditional public schools and 86 <a href="/wiki/Charter_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter schools">charter schools</a> as of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city\'s K-12 enrollment in district run schools dropped from 156,211 students in 2010 to 130,104 students in 2015. During the same time period, the enrollment in charter schools increased from 33,995 students in 2010 to 62,358 students in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> This consistent drop in enrollment led the city to close 24 of its public schools in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> During the 2014 school year, the city spent an average of $12,570 per pupil, below the average among comparable urban school districts.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Graduation rates among district-run schools, meanwhile, steadily increased in the ten years from 2005. In 2005, Philadelphia had a district graduation rate of 52%. This number increased to 65% in 2014, still below the national and state averages. Scores on the state\'s standardized test, the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_System_of_School_Assessment" title="Pennsylvania System of School Assessment">Pennsylvania System of School Assessment</a> (PSSA) trended upward from 2005 to 2011 but subsequently decreased. In 2005, the district-run schools scored an average of 37.4% on math and 35.5% on reading. The city\'s schools reached its peak scores in 2011 with 59.0% on math and 52.3% on reading. In 2014, the scores dropped significantly to 45.2% on math and 42.0% on reading.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of the city\'s public high schools, including charter schools, only four performed above the national average on the <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> (1497 out of 2400<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>) in 2014: <a href="/wiki/Julia_R._Masterman_School" title="Julia R. Masterman School">Masterman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_High_School_(Philadelphia)" title="Central High School (Philadelphia)">Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Girard_Academic_Music_Program" title="Girard Academic Music Program">Girard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MaST_Community_Charter_School" title="MaST Community Charter School">MaST Community Charter School</a>. All other district-run schools were below average.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Penn_campus_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Penn_campus_2.jpg/220px-Penn_campus_2.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Penn_campus_2.jpg/330px-Penn_campus_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Penn_campus_2.jpg/440px-Penn_campus_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="541" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Penn_campus_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Quadrangle at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>, one of the highest ranked universities in the world</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Pennsylvania_Medical_Hall_and_College_Hall_1842.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/University_of_Pennsylvania_Medical_Hall_and_College_Hall_1842.png/220px-University_of_Pennsylvania_Medical_Hall_and_College_Hall_1842.png" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/University_of_Pennsylvania_Medical_Hall_and_College_Hall_1842.png/330px-University_of_Pennsylvania_Medical_Hall_and_College_Hall_1842.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/University_of_Pennsylvania_Medical_Hall_and_College_Hall_1842.png/440px-University_of_Pennsylvania_Medical_Hall_and_College_Hall_1842.png 2x" data-file-width="1075" data-file-height="786" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Pennsylvania_Medical_Hall_and_College_Hall_1842.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Perelman_School_of_Medicine_at_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Perelman School of Medicine at the University of Pennsylvania">Perelman School of Medicine</a>, the oldest medical school in the United States</div></div></div>\n<p>Philadelphia has the third-largest student concentration on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a>, with over 120,000 college and university students enrolled within the city and nearly 300,000 in the metropolitan area.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> There are over 80 colleges, universities, trade, and specialty schools in the Philadelphia region. One of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> is in the city, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> institution with claims to being the oldest university in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city\'s largest school by number of students is <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple University</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Drexel_University" title="Drexel University">Drexel University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The University of Pennsylvania, Temple University and Drexel University comprise the city\'s major research universities. Philadelphia is also home to five schools of medicine: <a href="/wiki/Drexel_University_College_of_Medicine" title="Drexel University College of Medicine">Drexel University College of Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perelman_School_of_Medicine_at_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Perelman School of Medicine at the University of Pennsylvania">Perelman School of Medicine at the University of Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_College_of_Osteopathic_Medicine" title="Philadelphia College of Osteopathic Medicine">Philadelphia College of Osteopathic Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temple_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Temple University School of Medicine">Temple University School of Medicine</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson_University" title="Thomas Jefferson University">Thomas Jefferson University</a>. Hospitals, universities, and higher education research institutions in Philadelphia\'s four congressional districts received more than $252 million in <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> grants in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other institutions of higher learning within the city\'s borders include:\n</p>\n<table>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Community_College_of_Philadelphia" title="Community College of Philadelphia">Community College of Philadelphia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_University" title="Saint Joseph&#39;s University">Saint Joseph\'s University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Salle_University" title="La Salle University">La Salle University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson_University" title="Thomas Jefferson University">Thomas Jefferson University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_University" title="Philadelphia University">Philadelphia University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Chestnut_Hill_College" title="Chestnut Hill College">Chestnut Hill College</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Holy_Family_University" title="Holy Family University">Holy Family University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Peirce_College" title="Peirce College">Peirce College</a></li></ul>\n</td>\n<td valign="top">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Sciences" title="University of the Sciences">University of the Sciences</a></li>\n<li><a Institutes">The Art Institute of Philadelphia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Moore_College_of_Art_and_Design" title="Moore College of Art and Design">Moore College of Art and Design</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Academy_of_the_Fine_Arts" title="Pennsylvania Academy of the Fine Arts">Pennsylvania Academy of the Fine Arts</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Curtis_Institute_of_Music" title="Curtis Institute of Music">Curtis Institute of Music</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_Restaurant_School_at_Walnut_Hill_College" title="The Restaurant School at Walnut Hill College">The Restaurant School at Walnut Hill College</a></li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Philadelphia" title="Culture of Philadelphia">Culture of Philadelphia</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cultural_depictions_of_Philadelphia" title="Cultural depictions of Philadelphia">Cultural depictions of Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Historic_Landmarks_in_Philadelphia" title="List of National Historic Landmarks in Philadelphia">List of National Historic Landmarks in Philadelphia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_sites_of_interest_in_Philadelphia" title="List of sites of interest in Philadelphia">List of sites of interest in Philadelphia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Hall,_with_John_Barry_statue,_Philadelphia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Independence_Hall%2C_with_John_Barry_statue%2C_Philadelphia.jpg/170px-Independence_Hall%2C_with_John_Barry_statue%2C_Philadelphia.jpg" width="170" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Independence_Hall%2C_with_John_Barry_statue%2C_Philadelphia.jpg/255px-Independence_Hall%2C_with_John_Barry_statue%2C_Philadelphia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Independence_Hall%2C_with_John_Barry_statue%2C_Philadelphia.jpg/340px-Independence_Hall%2C_with_John_Barry_statue%2C_Philadelphia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1773" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Hall,_with_John_Barry_statue,_Philadelphia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Independence_Hall" title="Independence Hall">Independence Hall</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">Constitution</a> were adopted.</div></div></div>\n<p>Philadelphia is home to many <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Site_(United_States)" title="National Historic Site (United States)">national historical sites</a> that relate to the founding of the United States. <a href="/wiki/Independence_National_Historical_Park" title="Independence National Historical Park">Independence National Historical Park</a> is the center of these historical landmarks being one of the country\'s 22 <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>. <a href="/wiki/Independence_Hall" title="Independence Hall">Independence Hall</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> was signed, and the <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Bell" title="Liberty Bell">Liberty Bell</a> are the city\'s most famous attractions. Other national historic sites include the homes of <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe_National_Historic_Site" title="Edgar Allan Poe National Historic Site">Edgar Allan Poe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thaddeus_Kosciuszko_National_Memorial" title="Thaddeus Kosciuszko National Memorial">Thaddeus Kosciuszko</a>, early government buildings like the <a href="/wiki/First_Bank_of_the_United_States" title="First Bank of the United States">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Bank_of_the_United_States" title="Second Bank of the United States">Second Banks of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Mifflin" title="Fort Mifflin">Fort Mifflin</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Dei_(Old_Swedes%27)_Church" title="Gloria Dei (Old Swedes&#39;) Church">Gloria Dei (Old Swedes\') Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NHLP_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHLP-148">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia alone has 67 <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">National Historic Landmarks</a>, the third most of any city in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-NHLP_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHLP-148">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia\'s major science museums include the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Institute" title="Franklin Institute">Franklin Institute</a>, which contains the <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin_National_Memorial" title="Benjamin Franklin National Memorial">Benjamin Franklin National Memorial</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Natural_Sciences_of_Drexel_University" title="Academy of Natural Sciences of Drexel University">Academy of Natural Sciences</a>; the <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCtter_Museum" title="M\xc3\xbctter Museum">M\xc3\xbctter Museum</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania_Museum_of_Archaeology_and_Anthropology" title="University of Pennsylvania Museum of Archaeology and Anthropology">University of Pennsylvania Museum of Archaeology and Anthropology</a>. History museums include the <a href="/wiki/National_Constitution_Center" title="National Constitution Center">National Constitution Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_American_Revolution" title="Museum of the American Revolution">Museum of the American Revolution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_History_Museum" title="Philadelphia History Museum">Philadelphia History Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_American_Jewish_History" title="National Museum of American Jewish History">National Museum of American Jewish History</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_American_Museum_in_Philadelphia" title="African American Museum in Philadelphia">African American Museum in Philadelphia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Historical_Society_of_Pennsylvania" title="Historical Society of Pennsylvania">Historical Society of Pennsylvania</a>, the Masonic Library and Museum of Pennsylvania in the <a href="/wiki/Masonic_Temple_(Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania)" title="Masonic Temple (Philadelphia, Pennsylvania)">Masonic Temple</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_State_Penitentiary" title="Eastern State Penitentiary">Eastern State Penitentiary</a>. Philadelphia is home to the United States\' first <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Zoo" title="Philadelphia Zoo">zoo</a><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Hospital" title="Pennsylvania Hospital">hospital</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Fairmount_Park" title="Fairmount Park">Fairmount Park</a>, one of America\'s oldest and largest urban parks,<sup id="cite_ref-tplrank_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tplrank-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> founded in 1855.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is home to important archival repositories, including the <a href="/wiki/Library_Company_of_Philadelphia" title="Library Company of Philadelphia">Library Company of Philadelphia</a>, established in 1731 by <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Athenaeum_of_Philadelphia" title="Athenaeum of Philadelphia">Athenaeum of Philadelphia</a>, founded in 1814.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Historical_Society" title="Presbyterian Historical Society">Presbyterian Historical Society</a> is the country\'s oldest denominational historical society, organized in 1852.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_public_art_in_Philadelphia" title="List of public art in Philadelphia">List of public art in Philadelphia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Philadelphia_Art_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Philadelphia_Art_Museum.jpg/220px-Philadelphia_Art_Museum.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Philadelphia_Art_Museum.jpg/330px-Philadelphia_Art_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Philadelphia_Art_Museum.jpg/440px-Philadelphia_Art_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3886" data-file-height="2591" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Philadelphia_Art_Museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Museum_of_Art" title="Philadelphia Museum of Art">Philadelphia Museum of Art</a>, informally called the Art Museum</div></div></div>\n<p>The city contains many art museums, such as the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Academy_of_the_Fine_Arts" title="Pennsylvania Academy of the Fine Arts">Pennsylvania Academy of the Fine Arts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rodin_Museum" title="Rodin Museum">Rodin Museum</a>, which holds the largest collection of work by <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Rodin" title="Auguste Rodin">Auguste Rodin</a> outside France. The city\'s major art museum, the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Museum_of_Art" title="Philadelphia Museum of Art">Philadelphia Museum of Art</a>, is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_art_museums" title="List of largest art museums">largest art museums in the world</a>. The long flight of <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Steps" title="Rocky Steps">steps</a> to the Art Museum\'s main entrance became famous after the film <i><a href="/wiki/Rocky" title="Rocky">Rocky</a></i> (1976).<sup id="cite_ref-Dallasnews_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dallasnews-155">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is home to the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Sketch_Club" title="Philadelphia Sketch Club">Philadelphia Sketch Club</a>, one of the country\'s oldest artists\' clubs,<sup id="cite_ref-time_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-156">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Plastic_Club" title="The Plastic Club">The Plastic Club</a>, started by women excluded from the Sketch Club.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Many <a href="/wiki/Old_City,_Philadelphia" title="Old City, Philadelphia">Old City</a> art galleries stay open late on the <a href="/wiki/First_Friday_(public_event)" title="First Friday (public event)">First Friday</a> event of each month.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Annual events include <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Film_Festival" title="Philadelphia Film Festival">film festivals</a> and parades, the most famous being the <a href="/wiki/6abc_Dunkin%27_Donuts_Thanksgiving_Day_Parade" title="6abc Dunkin&#39; Donuts Thanksgiving Day Parade">Thanksgiving Day Parade</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mummers_Parade" title="Mummers Parade">Mummers Parade</a> on New Year\'s Day.\n</p><p>Areas such as South Street and Old City have a vibrant night life. The <a href="/wiki/Avenue_of_the_Arts_(Philadelphia)" title="Avenue of the Arts (Philadelphia)">Avenue of the Arts</a> in Center City contains many restaurants and theaters, such as the <a href="/wiki/Kimmel_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Kimmel Center for the Performing Arts">Kimmel Center for the Performing Arts</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Orchestra" title="Philadelphia Orchestra">Philadelphia Orchestra</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Music_(Philadelphia)" title="Academy of Music (Philadelphia)">Academy of Music</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Opera_Philadelphia" title="Opera Philadelphia">Opera Philadelphia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Ballet" title="Pennsylvania Ballet">Pennsylvania Ballet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dallasnews_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dallasnews-155">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Wilma_Theater_(Philadelphia)" title="Wilma Theater (Philadelphia)">Wilma Theatre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Theatre_Company" title="Philadelphia Theatre Company">Philadelphia Theatre Company</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Suzanne_Roberts_Theatre" title="Suzanne Roberts Theatre">Suzanne Roberts Theatre</a> produce a variety of new plays.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Several blocks to the east are the <a href="/wiki/Walnut_Street_Theatre" title="Walnut Street Theatre">Walnut Street Theatre</a>, claimed to be America\'s oldest and most subscribed-to theater in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Lantern_Theater_Company" title="Lantern Theater Company">Lantern Theater Company</a> at <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Episcopal_Church_(Philadelphia)" title="St. Stephen&#39;s Episcopal Church (Philadelphia)">St. Stephens Episcopal Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Keys_To_Community_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Keys_To_Community_crop.jpg/170px-Keys_To_Community_crop.jpg" width="170" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Keys_To_Community_crop.jpg/255px-Keys_To_Community_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Keys_To_Community_crop.jpg/340px-Keys_To_Community_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1677" data-file-height="2074" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Keys_To_Community_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Keys To Community</i>, a bust of <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Ben Franklin</a> by <a href="/wiki/James_Peniston" title="James Peniston">James Peniston</a>, 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>Philadelphia has more <a href="/wiki/Public_art" title="Public art">public art</a> than any other American city.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> In 1872, the <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Public_Art" title="Association for Public Art">Association for Public Art</a> (formerly the Fairmount Park Art Association) was created as the first private association in the United States dedicated to integrating public art and <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban planning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> In 1959, lobbying by the Artists Equity Association helped create the <a href="/wiki/Percent_for_Art" title="Percent for Art">Percent for Art</a> <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">ordinance</a>, the first for a U.S. city.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The program, which has funded more than 200 pieces of public art, is administered by the Philadelphia Office of Arts and Culture, the city\'s art agency.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia has more murals than any other U.S. city, thanks in part to the 1984 creation of the Department of Recreation\'s <a href="/wiki/Mural_Arts_Program" title="Mural Arts Program">Mural Arts Program</a>, which seeks to beautify neighborhoods and provide an outlet for <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a> artists. The program has funded more than 2,800 <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">murals</a> by professional, staff and volunteer artists and educated more than 20,000 youth in underserved neighborhoods throughout Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Philadelphia" title="Music of Philadelphia">Music of Philadelphia</a></div>\n<p>Philadelphia has played a prominent role in the <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_United_States" title="Music of the United States">music of the United States</a>. The culture of <a href="/wiki/American_popular_music" title="American popular music">American popular music</a> has been influenced by significant contributions of Philadelphia area musicians and producers, in both the recording and broadcasting industries. In 1952, the teen dance party program called <i>Bandstand</i> premiered on local television, hosted by <a href="/wiki/Bob_Horn_(broadcaster)" title="Bob Horn (broadcaster)">Bob Horn</a>. The show was renamed <i><a href="/wiki/American_Bandstand" title="American Bandstand">American Bandstand</a></i> in 1957 when it began national syndication on <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>, hosted by <a href="/wiki/Dick_Clark" title="Dick Clark">Dick Clark</a> and produced in Philadelphia until 1964 when it moved to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Promoters marketed youthful musical artists known as <a href="/wiki/Teen_idol" title="Teen idol">teen idols</a> to appeal to the young audience. Philadelphia-born singers such as <a href="/wiki/Frankie_Avalon" title="Frankie Avalon">Frankie Avalon</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Darren" title="James Darren">James Darren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Fisher_(singer)" title="Eddie Fisher (singer)">Eddie Fisher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Forte" title="Fabian Forte">Fabian Forte</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Rydell" title="Bobby Rydell">Bobby Rydell</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/South_Philadelphia" title="South Philadelphia">South Philly</a>-raised <a href="/wiki/Chubby_Checker" title="Chubby Checker">Chubby Checker</a>, topped the music charts, establishing a clean-cut <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> image.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_soul" title="Philadelphia soul">Philly soul</a> music of the late 1960s\xe2\x80\x931970s is a highly produced version of <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul music</a> which led to later forms of popular music such as <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary" title="Urban contemporary">urban contemporary</a> <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">rhythm and blues</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> On July 13, 1985, <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Stadium_(Philadelphia)" title="John F. Kennedy Stadium (Philadelphia)">John F. Kennedy Stadium</a> was the American venue for the <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> concert.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-170">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The city also hosted the <a href="/wiki/Live_8" title="Live 8">Live 8</a> concert, which attracted about 700,000 people to the <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin_Parkway" title="Benjamin Franklin Parkway">Benjamin Franklin Parkway</a> on July 2, 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Famous <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> musicians from Philadelphia or its suburbs include <a href="/wiki/Bill_Haley_%26_His_Comets" title="Bill Haley &amp; His Comets">Bill Haley &amp; His Comets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Todd_Rundgren" title="Todd Rundgren">Todd Rundgren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazz" title="Nazz">Nazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hall_%26_Oates" title="Hall &amp; Oates">Hall &amp; Oates</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hooters" title="The Hooters">The Hooters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ween" title="Ween">Ween</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(band)" title="Cinderella (band)">Cinderella</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pink_(singer)" title="Pink (singer)">Pink</a>. Local <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip-hop</a> artists include <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Jazzy_Jeff_%26_The_Fresh_Prince" title="DJ Jazzy Jeff &amp; The Fresh Prince">DJ Jazzy Jeff &amp; The Fresh Prince</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Goats" title="The Goats">The Goats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schoolly_D" title="Schoolly D">Schoolly D</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Lopes" title="Lisa Lopes">Lisa "Left Eye" Lopes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Institute_of_Music" title="Curtis Institute of Music">Curtis Institute of Music</a> is one of the world\'s premier <a href="/wiki/Music_school" title="Music school">conservatories</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Orchestra" title="Philadelphia Orchestra">Philadelphia Orchestra</a> is generally considered one of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Five_(orchestras)" title="Big Five (orchestras)">top five orchestras</a> in the United States. The orchestra performs at the <a href="/wiki/Kimmel_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Kimmel Center for the Performing Arts">Kimmel Center</a><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> and has a summer concert series at the <a href="/wiki/Mann_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Mann Center for the Performing Arts">Mann Center for the Performing Arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Opera_Philadelphia" title="Opera Philadelphia">Opera Philadelphia</a> performs at the nation\'s oldest continually operating opera house\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Music_(Philadelphia)" title="Academy of Music (Philadelphia)">Academy of Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dallasnews_155-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dallasnews-155">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The world-renowned <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Boys_Choir_%26_Chorale" title="Philadelphia Boys Choir &amp; Chorale">Philadelphia Boys Choir &amp; Chorale</a> has performed its music all over the world.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutus_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutus-174">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Philly_Pops" title="Philly Pops">Philly Pops</a> plays orchestral versions of popular <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swing_music" title="Swing music">swing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a> songs at the Kimmel Center and other venues within the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_(United_States)" title="Mid-Atlantic (United States)">mid-Atlantic</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-POPS_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POPS-175">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 186px"><div style="width: 186px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 184px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Curtisinstofmusic.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" class="gallerytext">\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Institute_of_Music" title="Curtis Institute of Music">Curtis Institute of Music</a>, one of the world\'s premier <a href="/wiki/Music_school" title="Music school">conservatories</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215.33333333333px"><div style="width: 215.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Kimmel_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Kimmel Center for the Performing Arts">Kimmel Center</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Orchestra" title="Philadelphia Orchestra">Philadelphia Orchestra</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215.33333333333px"><div style="width: 215.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 213.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Academy_of_Music,_Philadelphia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Academy_of_Music%2C_Philadelphia.jpg/320px-Academy_of_Music%2C_Philadelphia.jpg" width="214" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Academy_of_Music%2C_Philadelphia.jpg/480px-Academy_of_Music%2C_Philadelphia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Academy_of_Music%2C_Philadelphia.jpg/640px-Academy_of_Music%2C_Philadelphia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1688" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Music_(Philadelphia)" title="Academy of Music (Philadelphia)">Academy of Music</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Opera_Philadelphia" title="Opera Philadelphia">Opera Philadelphia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Ballet" title="Pennsylvania Ballet">Pennsylvania Ballet</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 200px"><div style="width: 200px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 198px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walnut_Street_Theatre_from_east.jpg" class="image"><img alt=""
