srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Walnut_Street_Theatre_from_east.jpg/445px-Walnut_Street_Theatre_from_east.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Walnut_Street_Theatre_from_east.jpg/594px-Walnut_Street_Theatre_from_east.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1980" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Walnut_Street_Theatre" title="Walnut Street Theatre">Walnut Street Theatre</a>, the oldest continuously operating <a href="/wiki/Theater_(structure)" title="Theater (structure)">theatre</a> in the English-speaking world\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 207.33333333333px"><div style="width: 207.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 205.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pennsylvania_Academy_of_Fine_Arts_-_Washington_Foyer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Pennsylvania_Academy_of_Fine_Arts_-_Washington_Foyer.jpg/308px-Pennsylvania_Academy_of_Fine_Arts_-_Washington_Foyer.jpg" width="206" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Pennsylvania_Academy_of_Fine_Arts_-_Washington_Foyer.jpg/461px-Pennsylvania_Academy_of_Fine_Arts_-_Washington_Foyer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Pennsylvania_Academy_of_Fine_Arts_-_Washington_Foyer.jpg/615px-Pennsylvania_Academy_of_Fine_Arts_-_Washington_Foyer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3712" data-file-height="2175" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>The atrium of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Academy_of_the_Fine_Arts" title="Pennsylvania Academy of the Fine Arts">Pennsylvania Academy of the Fine Arts</a>, the nation\'s oldest art school and art museum\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Philadelphia" title="Cuisine of Philadelphia">Cuisine of Philadelphia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pats_and_Genos.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Pats_and_Genos.jpg/220px-Pats_and_Genos.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Pats_and_Genos.jpg/330px-Pats_and_Genos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Pats_and_Genos.jpg/440px-Pats_and_Genos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1028" data-file-height="685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pats_and_Genos.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pat%27s_King_of_Steaks" title="Pat&#39;s King of Steaks">Pat\'s Steaks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geno%27s_Steaks" title="Geno&#39;s Steaks">Geno\'s Steaks</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The city is known for its <a href="/wiki/Submarine_sandwich" title="Submarine sandwich">hoagies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stromboli_(food)" title="Stromboli (food)">stromboli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scrapple" title="Scrapple">scrapple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pretzel#Pennsylvania" title="Pretzel">soft pretzels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_ice" title="Italian ice">water ice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_potato_candy" title="Irish potato candy">Irish potato candy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tastykake" title="Tastykake">Tastykakes</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cheesesteak" title="Cheesesteak">cheesesteak</a> sandwich which was developed by Italian immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The Philadelphia area has many establishments that serve cheesesteaks, including restaurants, <a href="/wiki/Tavern" title="Tavern">taverns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delicatessen" title="Delicatessen">delicatessens</a> and pizza parlors.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The originator of the thinly-sliced steak sandwich in the 1930s, initially without cheese, is <a href="/wiki/Pat%27s_King_of_Steaks" title="Pat&#39;s King of Steaks">Pat\'s King of Steaks</a>, which faces its rival <a href="/wiki/Geno%27s_Steaks" title="Geno&#39;s Steaks">Geno\'s Steaks</a>, founded in 1966,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> across the intersection of 9th Street and Passyunk Avenue in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Market,_Philadelphia" title="Italian Market, Philadelphia">Italian Market</a> of <a href="/wiki/South_Philadelphia" title="South Philadelphia">South Philadelphia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/McGillin%27s_Olde_Ale_House" title="McGillin&#39;s Olde Ale House">McGillin\'s Olde Ale House</a>, opened in 1860 on Drury Street in Center City, is the oldest continuously operated tavern in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/City_Tavern" title="City Tavern">City Tavern</a> is a replica of a historic 18th-century building first opened in 1773, demolished in 1854 after a fire, and rebuilt in 1975 on the same site as part of <a href="/wiki/Independence_National_Historical_Park" title="Independence National Historical Park">Independence National Historical Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The tavern offers authentic 18th-century recipes, served in seven period dining rooms, three wine cellar rooms and an outdoor garden.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Reading_Terminal_Market" title="Reading Terminal Market">Reading Terminal Market</a> is a historic <a href="/wiki/Marketplace" title="Marketplace">food market</a> founded in 1893 in the <a href="/wiki/Reading_Terminal" title="Reading Terminal">Reading Terminal</a> building, a designated National Historic Landmark. The enclosed market is one of the oldest and largest markets in the country, hosting over a hundred merchants offering <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Dutch" title="Pennsylvania Dutch">Pennsylvania Dutch</a> specialties, <a href="/wiki/Artisan_cheese" title="Artisan cheese">artisan cheese</a> and meat, locally grown groceries, and specialty and ethnic foods.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Philadelphia" title="Sports in Philadelphia">Sports in Philadelphia</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/U.S._cities_with_teams_from_four_major_league_sports" title="U.S. cities with teams from four major league sports">U.S. cities with teams from four major league sports</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Citizens_Bank_Park,_May_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg/220px-Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg/330px-Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg/440px-Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Citizens_Bank_Park,_May_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Citizens_Bank_Park" title="Citizens Bank Park">Citizens Bank Park</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Phillies</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Philadelphia\'s first professional sports team was baseball\'s <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Athletics_(1860%E2%80%9376)" title="Philadelphia Athletics (1860\xe2\x80\x9376)">Athletics</a>, organized in 1860.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The Athletics were initially an <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Base_Ball_Players" title="National Association of Base Ball Players">amateur league</a> team that <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Professional_Base_Ball_Players" title="National Association of Professional Base Ball Players">turned professional</a> in 1871, and then became a founding team of the current <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> in 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The city is one of 13 U.S. cities to have teams in <a href="/wiki/U.S._cities_with_teams_from_four_major_league_sports" title="U.S. cities with teams from four major league sports">all four major league sports</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Eagles" title="Philadelphia Eagles">Philadelphia Eagles</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Flyers" title="Philadelphia Flyers">Philadelphia Flyers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers" title="Philadelphia 76ers">Philadelphia 76ers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>. The Phillies, formed in 1883 as the Quakers and renamed in 1884,<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> are the oldest team continuously playing under the same name in the same city in the history of American professional sports.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Philadelphia metro area is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Union" title="Philadelphia Union">Philadelphia Union</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>. The Union began playing their home games at <a href="/wiki/Talen_Energy_Stadium" title="Talen Energy Stadium">Talen Energy Stadium</a> in 2010, a <a href="/wiki/Soccer-specific_stadium" title="Soccer-specific stadium">soccer-specific stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chester,_Pennsylvania" title="Chester, Pennsylvania">Chester, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WellsFargoCenterPhila_29.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/WellsFargoCenterPhila_29.JPG/220px-WellsFargoCenterPhila_29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/WellsFargoCenterPhila_29.JPG/330px-WellsFargoCenterPhila_29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/WellsFargoCenterPhila_29.JPG/440px-WellsFargoCenterPhila_29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WellsFargoCenterPhila_29.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Flyers" title="Philadelphia Flyers">Flyers</a> play at the <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Center_(Philadelphia)" title="Wells Fargo Center (Philadelphia)">Wells Fargo Center</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The city\'s professional teams and their fans endured 25 years without a championship, from the 76ers <a href="/wiki/1983_NBA_Finals" title="1983 NBA Finals">1983 NBA Finals</a> win<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> until the Phillies <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Series" title="2008 World Series">2008 World Series</a> win.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The lack of championships was sometimes attributed in jest to the <a href="/wiki/Curse_of_Billy_Penn" title="Curse of Billy Penn">Curse of Billy Penn</a> after <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Place#One_Liberty_Place" title="Liberty Place">One Liberty Place</a> became the first building to surpass the height of the <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">William Penn</a> statue on top of <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_City_Hall" title="Philadelphia City Hall">City Hall\'s</a> tower in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> After ten years passed without another championship, the Eagles won their first <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LII" title="Super Bowl LII">Super Bowl</a> in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> placed Philadelphia second on its list of The Fifteen Most Tortured Sports Cities.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Fans of the Eagles and Phillies were singled out as the worst fans in the country by <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i> magazine in 2011, which used the subtitle of "Meanest Fans in America" to summarize incidents of drunken behavior and a history of <a href="/wiki/Booing" title="Booing">booing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Major professional sports teams that originated in Philadelphia but which later moved to other cities include the <a href="/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors" title="Golden State Warriors">Golden State Warriors</a> basketball team\xe2\x80\x94in Philadelphia from 1946 to 1962<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94and the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> baseball team\xe2\x80\x94originally the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philadelphia_Athletics" title="History of the Philadelphia Athletics">Philadelphia Athletics</a> from 1901 to 1954 (a different Athletics team than the one mentioned above).<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia is home to professional, semi-professional, and elite amateur teams in <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> (<a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Fight" title="Philadelphia Fight">Philadelphia Fight</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>. Major running events in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Penn_Relays" title="Penn Relays">Penn Relays</a> (<a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Marathon" title="Philadelphia Marathon">Philadelphia Marathon</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Broad_Street_Run" title="Broad Street Run">Broad Street Run</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Cycling_Classic" title="Philadelphia International Cycling Classic">Philadelphia International Cycling Classic</a> was held annually from 1985 to 2016, but not in 2017 due to insufficient sponsorship.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Rugby_Championship" title="Collegiate Rugby Championship">Collegiate Rugby Championship</a> is played every June at <a href="/wiki/Talen_Energy_Stadium" title="Talen Energy Stadium">Talen Energy Stadium</a> in Chester, Pennsylvania.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A358,_Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania,_USA,_Boathouse_Row_at_night,_2009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/A358%2C_Philadelphia%2C_Pennsylvania%2C_USA%2C_Boathouse_Row_at_night%2C_2009.JPG/220px-A358%2C_Philadelphia%2C_Pennsylvania%2C_USA%2C_Boathouse_Row_at_night%2C_2009.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/A358%2C_Philadelphia%2C_Pennsylvania%2C_USA%2C_Boathouse_Row_at_night%2C_2009.JPG/330px-A358%2C_Philadelphia%2C_Pennsylvania%2C_USA%2C_Boathouse_Row_at_night%2C_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/A358%2C_Philadelphia%2C_Pennsylvania%2C_USA%2C_Boathouse_Row_at_night%2C_2009.JPG/440px-A358%2C_Philadelphia%2C_Pennsylvania%2C_USA%2C_Boathouse_Row_at_night%2C_2009.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="675" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A358,_Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania,_USA,_Boathouse_Row_at_night,_2009.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Historic <a href="/wiki/Boathouse_Row" title="Boathouse Row">Boathouse Row</a> at night on the <a href="/wiki/Schuylkill_River" title="Schuylkill River">Schuylkill</a>, a symbol of the city\'s rich rowing history</div></div></div>\n<p>Rowing has been popular in Philadelphia since the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-RWestcott_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RWestcott-204">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boathouse_Row" title="Boathouse Row">Boathouse Row</a> is a symbol of Philadelphia\'s rich rowing history, and each <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Big_5" title="Philadelphia Big 5">Big Five</a> member has its own boathouse.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia hosts numerous local and collegiate rowing clubs and competitions, including the annual <a href="/wiki/Dad_Vail_Regatta" title="Dad Vail Regatta">Dad Vail Regatta</a>, which is the largest <a href="/wiki/College_rowing_(United_States)" title="College rowing (United States)">intercollegiate rowing</a> event in North America with more than 100 U.S and Canadian colleges and universities participating;<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> the annual <a href="/wiki/Stotesbury_Cup" title="Stotesbury Cup">Stotesbury Cup Regatta</a>, which is billed as the world\'s oldest and largest rowing event for high school students;<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Schuylkill_Regatta" title="Head of the Schuylkill Regatta">Head of the Schuylkill Regatta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> The regattas are held on the <a href="/wiki/Schuylkill_River" title="Schuylkill River">Schuylkill River</a> and organized by the <a href="/wiki/Schuylkill_Navy" title="Schuylkill Navy">Schuylkill Navy</a>, an association of area rowing clubs that has produced numerous <a href="/wiki/Rowing_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Rowing at the Summer Olympics">Olympic rowers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Spinners" title="Philadelphia Spinners">Philadelphia Spinners</a> were a professional <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_(sport)" title="Ultimate (sport)">ultimate</a> team in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Ultimate" title="Major League Ultimate">Major League Ultimate</a> (MLU) until 2016. The Spinners were one of the original eight teams of the <a href="/wiki/American_Ultimate_Disc_League" title="American Ultimate Disc League">American Ultimate Disc League</a> (AUDL) that began in 2012. They played at <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Field" title="Franklin Field">Franklin Field</a> and won the inaugural AUDL championship and the final MLU championship in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> The MLU was suspended indefinitely by its investors in December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phoenix_(AUDL)" title="Philadelphia Phoenix (AUDL)">Philadelphia Phoenix</a> continue to play in the AUDL.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia is home to the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Big_5" title="Philadelphia Big 5">Philadelphia Big 5</a>, a group of five <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a> college basketball programs. The Big 5 are <a href="/wiki/La_Salle_University" title="La Salle University">La Salle</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">Penn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_University" title="Saint Joseph&#39;s University">Saint Joseph\'s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Villanova_University" title="Villanova University">Villanova</a> universities.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> The sixth NCAA Division I school in Philadelphia is <a href="/wiki/Drexel_University" title="Drexel University">Drexel University</a>. Villanova won the <a href="/wiki/2016_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2016 NCAA Division I Men&#39;s Basketball Tournament">2016</a><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2018_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2018 NCAA Division I Men&#39;s Basketball Tournament">2018</a><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> championship of the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="NCAA Division I Men&#39;s Basketball Tournament">NCAA Division I Men\'s Basketball Tournament</a>.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">Team\n</th>\n<th scope="col">League\n</th>\n<th href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Union" title="Philadelphia Union">Philadelphia Union</a>\n</th>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">MLS</a>\n</td>\n<td>Soccer\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Talen_Energy_Stadium" title="Talen Energy Stadium">Talen Energy Stadium</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center">18,500\n</td>\n<td align="center">2010\n</td>\n<td>none\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">Parks</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Detroit_Photographic_Company_(0757).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280757%29.jpg/220px-Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280757%29.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280757%29.jpg/330px-Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280757%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280757%29.jpg/440px-Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280757%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1201" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Detroit_Photographic_Company_(0757).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fairmount Park, ca. 1900</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fairmount_Park" title="Fairmount Park">Fairmount Park</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_parks_in_Philadelphia" title="List of parks in Philadelphia">List of parks in Philadelphia</a></div>\n<p>As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the total city parkland, including municipal, state and federal parks within the city limits, amounts to 11,211 acres (17.5&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-tplrank_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tplrank-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia\'s largest park is <a href="/wiki/Fairmount_Park" title="Fairmount Park">Fairmount Park</a> which includes the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Zoo" title="Philadelphia Zoo">Philadelphia Zoo</a> and encompasses 2,052 acres (3.2&#160;sq&#160;mi) of the total parkland, while the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Wissahickon_Valley_Park" title="Wissahickon Valley Park">Wissahickon Valley Park</a> contains 2,042 acres (3.2&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-parkacres_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parkacres-217">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Fairmount Park, when combined with Wissahickon Valley Park, is one of the largest contiguous <a href="/wiki/Urban_park" title="Urban park">urban park</a> areas in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-tplrank_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tplrank-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The two parks, along with the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Revival_architecture" title="Colonial Revival architecture">Colonial Revival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federal_architecture" title="Federal architecture">Federal</a>-style <a href="/wiki/List_of_houses_in_Fairmount_Park" title="List of houses in Fairmount Park">mansions</a> contained in them, have been listed as one entity on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> since 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-NRHP_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRHP-218">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Hall_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Independence_Hall_4.jpg/220px-Independence_Hall_4.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Independence_Hall_4.jpg/330px-Independence_Hall_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Independence_Hall_4.jpg/440px-Independence_Hall_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Hall_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Old_City_Hall_(Philadelphia)" title="Old City Hall (Philadelphia)">Old City Hall</a> served as Philadelphia\'s town hall from 1800 to 1854.</div></div></div>\n<p>From a governmental perspective, Philadelphia County is a <a href="/wiki/Legal_nullity" title="Legal nullity">legal nullity</a>, as all county functions were assumed by the city in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-Charter_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charter-219">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The city has been coterminous with the county since 1854.<sup id="cite_ref-Consolidation_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Consolidation-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia\'s 1952 <a href="/wiki/Home_Rule" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Rule">Home Rule</a> <a href="/wiki/Municipal_charter" title="Municipal charter">Charter</a> was written by the City Charter Commission, which was created by the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_General_Assembly" title="Pennsylvania General Assembly">Pennsylvania General Assembly</a> in an act of April 21, 1949, and a city ordinance of June 15, 1949. The existing <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">city council</a> received a proposed draft on February 14, 1951, and the electors approved it in an election held April 17, 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-PHRC_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PHRC-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> The first elections under the new Home Rule Charter were held in November 1951, and the newly elected officials took office in January 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-Charter_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charter-219">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city uses the <a href="/wiki/Mayor%E2%80%93council_government#Strong-mayor_form" title="Mayor\xe2\x80\x93council government">strong-mayor</a> version of the mayor\xe2\x80\x93council form of government, which is led by one <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> in whom executive authority is vested. The mayor has the authority to appoint and dismiss members of all boards and commissions without the approval of the city council. Elected <a href="/wiki/At-large" title="At-large">at-large</a>, the mayor is limited to two consecutive four-year terms, but can run for the position again after an intervening term.<sup id="cite_ref-PHRC_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PHRC-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse.jpg/170px-James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse.jpg" width="170" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse.jpg/255px-James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse.jpg/340px-James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2361" data-file-height="2814" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse" title="James A. Byrne United States Courthouse">James A. Byrne United States Courthouse</a>, houses the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Third_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit</a><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Eastern_District_of_Pennsylvania" title="United States District Court for the Eastern District of Pennsylvania">United States District Court for the Eastern District of Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Courts">Courts</span></h3>\n<p>The Philadelphia County <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_courts_of_common_pleas" title="Pennsylvania courts of common pleas">Court of Common Pleas</a> (the First Judicial District of Pennsylvania) is the <a href="/wiki/Trial_court" title="Trial court">trial court</a> of general jurisdiction for the city, hearing <a href="/wiki/Felony" title="Felony">felony</a>-level criminal cases and civil suits above the minimum jurisdictional limit of $10,000. The court also has <a href="/wiki/Appellate_jurisdiction" title="Appellate jurisdiction">appellate jurisdiction</a> over rulings from the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Municipal_Court" title="Philadelphia Municipal Court">Municipal</a> and Traffic Courts, and some administrative agencies and boards. The trial division has 70 commissioned judges elected by the voters, along with about one thousand other employees.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The court also has a family division with 25 judges<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> and an orphans\' court with three judges.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the city\'s <a href="/wiki/District_Attorney_of_Philadelphia" title="District Attorney of Philadelphia">District Attorney</a> is <a href="/wiki/Larry_Krasner" title="Larry Krasner">Larry Krasner</a>, a Democrat.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> The last Republican to hold the office is <a href="/wiki/Ronald_D._Castille" title="Ronald D. Castille">Ronald D. Castille</a>, who left in 1991 and later served as the Chief Justice of the Pennsylvania Supreme Court from 2008 to 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Municipal_Court" title="Philadelphia Municipal Court">Philadelphia Municipal Court</a> handles misdemeanor and felony criminal cases with maximum incarceration of five years, and civil cases involving $12,000 or less ($15,000 in real estate and school tax cases), and all landlord-tenant disputes. The municipal court has 27 judges elected by the voters.<sup id="cite_ref-Municipal_Court_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Municipal_Court-228">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia <a href="/wiki/Traffic_court" title="Traffic court">Traffic Court</a> is a court of special jurisdiction that hears violations of traffic laws.<sup id="cite_ref-Traffic_Court_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Traffic_Court-229">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> As with magisterial district judges, the judges need not be lawyers, but must complete the certifying course and pass the qualifying examination administered by the Minor Judiciary Education Board.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pennsylvania\'s three <a href="/wiki/Appellate_court" title="Appellate court">appellate courts</a> also have sittings in Philadelphia. The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Pennsylvania" title="Supreme Court of Pennsylvania">Supreme Court of Pennsylvania</a>, the court of last resort in the state, regularly hears arguments in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_City_Hall" title="Philadelphia City Hall">Philadelphia City Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Superior_Court_of_Pennsylvania" title="Superior Court of Pennsylvania">Superior Court of Pennsylvania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Court_of_Pennsylvania" title="Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania">Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania</a> also sit in Philadelphia several times a year.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Judges for these courts are elected at large.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> The state Supreme Court and Superior Court have deputy <a href="/wiki/Prothonotary" title="Prothonotary">prothonotary</a> offices in Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Additionally, Philadelphia is home to the federal <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Eastern_District_of_Pennsylvania" title="United States District Court for the Eastern District of Pennsylvania">United States District Court for the Eastern District of Pennsylvania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Third_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit">Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit</a>, both of which are housed in the <a href="/wiki/James_A._Byrne_United_States_Courthouse" title="James A. Byrne United States Courthouse">James A. Byrne United States Courthouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Philadelphia" title="List of mayors of Philadelphia">List of mayors of Philadelphia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_County,_Pennsylvania#Politics" title="Philadelphia County, Pennsylvania">Philadelphia County, Pennsylvania \xc2\xa7&#160;Politics</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Philadelphia_Mayor_Jim_Kenney_(25550370434).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Philadelphia_Mayor_Jim_Kenney_%2825550370434%29.jpg/220px-Philadelphia_Mayor_Jim_Kenney_%2825550370434%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Philadelphia_Mayor_Jim_Kenney_%2825550370434%29.jpg/330px-Philadelphia_Mayor_Jim_Kenney_%2825550370434%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Philadelphia_Mayor_Jim_Kenney_%2825550370434%29.jpg/440px-Philadelphia_Mayor_Jim_Kenney_%2825550370434%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Philadelphia_Mayor_Jim_Kenney_(25550370434).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jim_Kenney" title="Jim Kenney">Jim Kenney</a>, the current and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Philadelphia" title="List of mayors of Philadelphia">99th Mayor of Philadelphia</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The current mayor is <a href="/wiki/Jim_Kenney" title="Jim Kenney">Jim Kenney</a> who won the election in November, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenney_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenney-240">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Kenney\'s predecessor was <a href="/wiki/Michael_Nutter" title="Michael Nutter">Michael Nutter</a> who had served two terms from 2009 to January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Nutter_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nutter-241">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> Kenney is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Democratic_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Democratic Party">Democratic Party</a> as all <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Philadelphia#Mayors" title="List of mayors of Philadelphia">Philadelphia mayors</a> have been since 1952. <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_City_Council" title="Philadelphia City Council">Philadelphia City Council</a> is the legislative branch which consists of ten council members representing individual districts and seven members elected <a href="/wiki/At-large" title="At-large">at-large</a>, all of whom are elected to four-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Democrats currently hold 14 seats including nine of the ten districts and five at-large seats, while Republicans hold two at-large seats and the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Philadelphia" title="Northeast Philadelphia">Northeast-based</a> Tenth District. The current council president is <a href="/wiki/Darrell_L._Clarke" title="Darrell L. Clarke">Darrell L. Clarke</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of December 31, 2016, there were 1,102,620 registered voters in Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-Registration_2016_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Registration_2016-244">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Registered voters constitute 70.3% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;h&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>: 853,140 (77.4%)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>: 125,530 (11.4%)</li>\n<li>Other parties and unaffiliated: 123,950 (11.2%)<sup id="cite_ref-Registration_2016_244-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Registration_2016-244">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<table class="wikitable floatright" align="center" style="font-size: 95%;">\n<caption><b>Presidential Elections Results</b><sup id="cite_ref-elections_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elections-246">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr bgcolor="lightgrey">\n<th>Year\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Third_Party_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Party (United States)">Third Parties</a>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Pennsylvania,_2016" title="United States presidential election in Pennsylvania, 2016">2016</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6">15.3% <i>108,748</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b>82.3%</b> <i>584,025</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">2.4% <i>16,845</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Pennsylvania,_2012" title="United States presidential election in Pennsylvania, 2012">2012</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6">14.0% <i>96,467</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b>85.2%</b> <i>588,806</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">0.8% <i>5,503</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Pennsylvania,_2008" title="United States presidential election in Pennsylvania, 2008">2008</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6">16.3% <i>117,221</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b>83.0%</b> <i>595,980</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">0.7% <i>4,824</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Pennsylvania,_2004" title="United States presidential election in Pennsylvania, 2004">2004</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6">19.3% <i>130,099</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b>80.4%</b> <i>542,205</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">0.3% <i>1,765</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Pennsylvania,_2000" title="United States presidential election in Pennsylvania, 2000">2000</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6">18.0% <i>100,959</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b>80.0%</b> <i>449,182</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">2.0% <i>11,039</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td>...\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Pennsylvania,_1936" title="United States presidential election in Pennsylvania, 1936">1936</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6">36.9% <i>329,881</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF"><b>60.5%</b> <i>539,757</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">2.6% <i>23,310</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Pennsylvania,_1932" title="United States presidential election in Pennsylvania, 1932">1932</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6"><b>54.5%</b> <i>331,092</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF">42.9% <i>260,276</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">2.6% <i>15,651</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td>...\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Pennsylvania,_1892" title="United States presidential election in Pennsylvania, 1892">1892</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6"><b>57.5%</b> <i>116,685</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF">41.6% <i>84,470</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">1.0% <i>1,947</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6"><b><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Pennsylvania,_1888" title="United States presidential election in Pennsylvania, 1888">1888</a></b>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFB6B6"><b>54.2%</b> <i>111,358</i>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#B0CEFF">45.2% <i>92,786</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:honeyDew;">0.6% <i>1,300</i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Philadelphia was a bastion of the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> from the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> until the mid-1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> The city hosted the first <a href="/wiki/Republican_National_Convention" title="Republican National Convention">Republican National Convention</a> in <a href="/wiki/1856_Republican_National_Convention" title="1856 Republican National Convention">1856</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Democratic registrations increased after the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>; however, the city was not carried by Democrat <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> in his landslide victory of <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1932" title="United States presidential election, 1932">1932</a> as Pennsylvania was one of only six states won by Republican <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hoover" title="Herbert Hoover">Herbert Hoover</a>. Voter turnout surged from 600,000 in 1932 to nearly 900,000 in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1936" title="United States presidential election, 1936">1936</a> and Roosevelt carried Philadelphia with over 60% of the vote. The city has voted Democratic in every presidential election since 1936. In <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008</a>, Democrat <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> drew 83% of the city\'s vote. Obama\'s win was even greater in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">2012</a>, capturing 85% of the vote. In <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">2016</a>, Democrat <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> won 82% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-elections_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elections-246">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of the declining population in the city and state,<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia has only three <a href="/wiki/Congressional_district" title="Congressional district">congressional districts</a> of the 18 districts in Pennsylvania, based on the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a> apportionment:<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="Pennsylvania&#39;s 1st congressional district">the 1st district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Bob_Brady" title="Bob Brady">Bob Brady</a>; <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Pennsylvania&#39;s 2nd congressional district">the 2nd</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Evans_(politician)" title="Dwight Evans (politician)">Dwight Evans</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_13th_congressional_district" title="Pennsylvania&#39;s 13th congressional district">the 13th</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Boyle" title="Brendan Boyle">Brendan Boyle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> All three representatives are Democrats though Republicans still have some support in the city, primarily in the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Philadelphia" title="Northeast Philadelphia">Northeast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sam_Katz_(Philadelphia)" title="Sam Katz (Philadelphia)">Sam Katz</a> ran competitive mayoral races as the Republican nominee in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_mayoral_election,_1999" title="Philadelphia mayoral election, 1999">1999</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_mayoral_election,_2003" title="Philadelphia mayoral election, 2003">2003</a>, losing to Democrat <a href="/wiki/John_F._Street" title="John F. Street">John Street</a> both times.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pennsylvania\'s longest-serving <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Senators_from_Pennsylvania" title="List of United States Senators from Pennsylvania">Senator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arlen_Specter" title="Arlen Specter">Arlen Specter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>  was an <a href="/wiki/Alumnus" title="Alumnus">alumnus</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a> who opened his first law practice in Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-SpecterBio_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpecterBio-257">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> Specter served as a Republican from 1981 and as a Democrat from 2009, losing that party\'s primary in <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Democratic_primary_election_in_Pennsylvania,_2010" title="United States Senate Democratic primary election in Pennsylvania, 2010">2010</a> and leaving office in January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> He had also been assistant counsel on the <a href="/wiki/Warren_Commission" title="Warren Commission">Warren Commission</a> in 1964 and the city\'s district attorney from 1966 to 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-SpecterBio_257-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpecterBio-257">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia has hosted various <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_nominating_convention" title="United States presidential nominating convention">national conventions</a>, including in <a href="/wiki/1848_Whig_National_Convention" title="1848 Whig National Convention">1848 (Whig)</a>, <a href="/wiki/1856_Republican_National_Convention" title="1856 Republican National Convention">1856 (Republican)</a>, <a href="/wiki/1872_Republican_National_Convention" title="1872 Republican National Convention">1872 (Republican)</a>, <a href="/wiki/1900_Republican_National_Convention" title="1900 Republican National Convention">1900 (Republican)</a>, <a href="/wiki/1936_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1936 Democratic National Convention">1936 (Democratic)</a>, <a href="/wiki/1940_Republican_National_Convention" title="1940 Republican National Convention">1940 (Republican)</a>, <a href="/wiki/1948_Republican_National_Convention" title="1948 Republican National Convention">1948 (Republican)</a>, <a href="/wiki/1948_Progressive_National_Convention" title="1948 Progressive National Convention">1948 (Progressive)</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000_Republican_National_Convention" title="2000 Republican National Convention">2000 (Republican)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2016_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2016 Democratic National Convention">2016 (Democratic)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gtmadonna_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gtmadonna-259">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia has been home to one <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">vice president</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_M._Dallas" title="George M. Dallas">George M. Dallas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> and one Civil War general, <a href="/wiki/George_B._McClellan" title="George B. McClellan">George B. McClellan</a>, who won his party\'s nomination for <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">president</a> but lost in the general election to <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> in 1864.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Philadelphia" title="Crime in Philadelphia">Crime in Philadelphia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Philadelphia_Police_Headquarters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Philadelphia_Police_Headquarters.jpg/220px-Philadelphia_Police_Headquarters.jpg" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Philadelphia_Police_Headquarters.jpg/330px-Philadelphia_Police_Headquarters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Philadelphia_Police_Headquarters.jpg/440px-Philadelphia_Police_Headquarters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3178" data-file-height="1613" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Philadelphia_Police_Headquarters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Police Administration Building (the Roundhouse) in Center City east of <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Philadelphia" title="Chinatown, Philadelphia">Chinatown</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Police_Department#Districts" title="Philadelphia Police Department">police districts</a> with the highest rates of violent crime are <a href="/wiki/Frankford,_Philadelphia" title="Frankford, Philadelphia">Frankford</a> (15th district) and <a href="/wiki/Kensington,_Philadelphia" title="Kensington, Philadelphia">Kensington</a> (24th district) in the <a href="/wiki/Near_Northeast_Philadelphia" title="Near Northeast Philadelphia">Near Northeast</a>, and districts to the <a href="/wiki/North_Philadelphia" title="North Philadelphia">North</a> (22nd, 25th, and 35th districts), <a href="/wiki/West_Philadelphia" title="West Philadelphia">West</a> (19th district) and <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Philadelphia" title="Southwest Philadelphia">Southwest</a> (12th district) of <a href="/wiki/Center_City,_Philadelphia" title="Center City, Philadelphia">Center City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia had 525 murders in 1990, a rate of 31.5 per 100,000. An average of about 600 murders occurred each year for most of the 1990s. The murder count dropped in 2002 to 288, then rose to 406 by 2006, before dropping slightly to 392 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> A few years later, Philadelphia began to see a rapid decline in homicides and violent crime. In 2013, the city had 246 murders, which is a decrease of nearly 40% since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, 248 homicides were committed. The homicide rate rose to 280 in 2015, then fell slightly to 277 in 2016, before rising again to 317 in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-phillypolice.com_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phillypolice.com-264">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, Philadelphia\'s homicide rate of 27.7 per 100,000 people was the highest of the country\'s 10 most populous cities.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Philadelphia had the fourth-highest homicide rate among the country\'s most populous cities. The rate dropped to 16 homicides per 100,000 residents by 2014 placing Philadelphia as the sixth-highest city in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MOUNTED_POLICEMAN_ON_BUSY_DOWNTOWN_THOROUGHFARE_-_NARA_-_552732_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/MOUNTED_POLICEMAN_ON_BUSY_DOWNTOWN_THOROUGHFARE_-_NARA_-_552732_b.jpg/220px-MOUNTED_POLICEMAN_ON_BUSY_DOWNTOWN_THOROUGHFARE_-_NARA_-_552732_b.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/MOUNTED_POLICEMAN_ON_BUSY_DOWNTOWN_THOROUGHFARE_-_NARA_-_552732_b.jpg/330px-MOUNTED_POLICEMAN_ON_BUSY_DOWNTOWN_THOROUGHFARE_-_NARA_-_552732_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/MOUNTED_POLICEMAN_ON_BUSY_DOWNTOWN_THOROUGHFARE_-_NARA_-_552732_b.jpg/440px-MOUNTED_POLICEMAN_ON_BUSY_DOWNTOWN_THOROUGHFARE_-_NARA_-_552732_b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2678" data-file-height="1785" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MOUNTED_POLICEMAN_ON_BUSY_DOWNTOWN_THOROUGHFARE_-_NARA_-_552732_b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mounted_police" title="Mounted police">Mounted police officer</a> in Center City, 1973</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2004, there were 7,513.5 crimes per 200,000 people in Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Among its neighboring mid-Atlantic cities in the same population group, <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a> and Washington, D.C. were ranked second- and third-most dangerous cities in the United States, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Morgan_Quitno_Rankings_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan_Quitno_Rankings-267">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">Camden</a>, New Jersey, a city directly across the Delaware River from Center City, was ranked as the most dangerous city in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Morgan_Quitno_Rankings_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan_Quitno_Rankings-267">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The number of shootings in the city has declined significantly since the early years of the 21st century. Shooting incidents peaked at 1,857 in 2006 before declining nearly 44 percent to 1,047 shootings in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Major crimes have decreased gradually since a peak in 2006 when 85,498 major crimes were reported. The number of reported major crimes fell 11 percent in three years to 68,815 occurrences in 2014. <a href="/wiki/Violent_crime" title="Violent crime">Violent crimes</a>, which include homicide, rape, aggravated assault, and robbery, decreased 14 percent in three years to 15,771 occurrences in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-State_of_the_City_2015_110-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_City_2015-110">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia was ranked as the 76th most dangerous city in a 2018 report based on <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> data from 2016 for the rate of violent crimes per 1,000 residents in American cities with 25,000 or more people.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> The latest four years of reports indicate a steady reduction in violent crime as the city placed 67th in the 2017 report,<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> 65th in 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> and 54th in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, Philadelphia decriminalized small amounts of marijuana, reducing penalties for possession and public use to minor fines and community service. The move makes Philadelphia the largest city in the United States to decriminalize pot.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Philadelphia" title="Media in Philadelphia">Media in Philadelphia</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inquirerbldg_sign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Inquirerbldg_sign.jpg/220px-Inquirerbldg_sign.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Inquirerbldg_sign.jpg/330px-Inquirerbldg_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Inquirerbldg_sign.jpg/440px-Inquirerbldg_sign.jpg 2x" data-file-width="838" data-file-height="558" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inquirerbldg_sign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Inquirer_Building" title="Inquirer Building">Inquirer Building</a> - the newspaper\'s home until 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>Philadelphia\'s two major <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">daily newspapers</a> are <i><a href="/wiki/The_Philadelphia_Inquirer" title="The Philadelphia Inquirer">The Philadelphia Inquirer</a></i>, first published in 1829\xe2\x80\x94the third-oldest surviving daily newspaper in the country\xe2\x80\x94and the <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Daily_News" title="Philadelphia Daily News">Philadelphia Daily News</a></i>, first published in 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-Pressa_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pressa-273">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Daily News</i> has been published as an edition of the <i>Inquirer</i> since 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> Recent owners of the <i>Inquirer</i> and <i>Daily News</i> have included <a href="/wiki/Knight_Ridder" title="Knight Ridder">Knight Ridder</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_McClatchy_Company" title="The McClatchy Company">The McClatchy Company</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Media_Holdings" title="Philadelphia Media Holdings">Philadelphia Media Holdings</a>, with the latter organization declaring bankruptcy in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Philadelphia_Newspapers_Sold_Yet_Again_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philadelphia_Newspapers_Sold_Yet_Again-275">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> After two years of financial struggle, the newspapers were sold to <a href="/wiki/Interstate_General_Media" title="Interstate General Media">Interstate General Media</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Philadelphia_Newspapers_Sold_Yet_Again_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philadelphia_Newspapers_Sold_Yet_Again-275">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> The two newspapers had a combined daily circulation of 306,831 and a Sunday circulation of 477,313 in 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94the eighteenth largest circulation in the country\xe2\x80\x94while the website of the newspapers, Philly.com,<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> was ranked thirteenth in popularity among online U.S. newspapers by <a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">Alexa Internet</a> for the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-circulation_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circulation-277">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Smaller publications include the <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Tribune" title="Philadelphia Tribune">Philadelphia Tribune</a></i> published five days each week for the <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African-American</a> community;<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_(magazine)" title="Philadelphia (magazine)">Philadelphia</a></i> magazine, a monthly regional magazine;<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Weekly" title="Philadelphia Weekly">Philadelphia Weekly</a></i>, a weekly alternative newspaper;<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Gay_News" title="Philadelphia Gay News">Philadelphia Gay News</a></i>, a weekly newspaper for the <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> community;<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jewish_Exponent" title="The Jewish Exponent">The Jewish Exponent</a></i>, a weekly newspaper for the <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> community;<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Al_D%C3%ADa_(Philadelphia)" title="Al D\xc3\xada (Philadelphia)">Al D\xc3\xada</a></i>, a weekly newspaper for the <a href="/wiki/Latino" title="Latino">Latino</a> community;<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia Metro">Philadelphia Metro</a></i>, a free daily newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Student-run newspapers include the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Pennsylvanian" title="The Daily Pennsylvanian">The Daily Pennsylvanian</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple University</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Temple_News" title="The Temple News">The Temple News</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Drexel_University" title="Drexel University">Drexel University</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Triangle_(newspaper)" title="The Triangle (newspaper)">The Triangle</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span></h3>\n<p>The first experimental radio license was issued in Philadelphia in August 1912 to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_University" title="Saint Joseph&#39;s University">St. Joseph\'s College</a>. The first <a href="/wiki/Commercial_broadcasting" title="Commercial broadcasting">commercial</a> <a href="/wiki/AM_broadcasting" title="AM broadcasting">AM</a> radio stations began broadcasting in 1922: first <a href="/wiki/WTEL_(AM)" title="WTEL (AM)">WIP</a>, then owned by <a href="/wiki/Gimbels" title="Gimbels">Gimbels</a> department store, followed by <a href="/wiki/WFIL" title="WFIL">WFIL</a>, then owned by <a href="/wiki/Strawbridge%27s" title="Strawbridge&#39;s">Strawbridge &amp; Clothier</a> department store, and WOO, a defunct station owned by <a href="/wiki/Wanamaker%27s" title="Wanamaker&#39;s">Wanamaker\'s</a> department store, as well as <a href="/wiki/WPHT" title="WPHT">WCAU</a> and <a href="/wiki/WDAS_(AM)" title="WDAS (AM)">WDAS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Media_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Media-288">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">FCC</a> lists 28 <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a> and 11 AM stations for Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> As of December 2017, the ten highest-rated stations in Philadelphia were <a href="/wiki/Adult_contemporary_music" title="Adult contemporary music">adult contemporary</a> <a href="/wiki/WBEB" title="WBEB">WBEB-FM</a> (101.1), <a href="/wiki/Sports_radio" title="Sports radio">sports talk</a> <a href="/wiki/WIP-FM" title="WIP-FM">WIP-FM</a> (94.1), <a href="/wiki/Classic_rock" title="Classic rock">classic rock</a> <a href="/wiki/WMGK" title="WMGK">WMGK-FM</a> (102.9), <a href="/wiki/Urban_adult_contemporary" title="Urban adult contemporary">urban adult contemporary</a> <a href="/wiki/WDAS-FM" title="WDAS-FM">WDAS-FM</a> (105.3), <a href="/wiki/Classic_hits" title="Classic hits">classic hits</a> <a href="/wiki/WOGL" title="WOGL">WOGL-FM</a> (98.1), <a href="/wiki/Album-oriented_rock" title="Album-oriented rock">album-oriented rock</a> <a href="/wiki/WMMR" title="WMMR">WMMR-FM</a> (93.3), <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country music</a> <a href="/wiki/WXTU" title="WXTU">WXTU-FM</a> (92.5), <a href="/wiki/All-news_radio" title="All-news radio">all-news</a> <a href="/wiki/KYW_(AM)" title="KYW (AM)">KYW-AM</a> (1060), <a href="/wiki/Talk_radio" title="Talk radio">talk radio</a> <a href="/wiki/WHYY-FM" title="WHYY-FM">WHYY-FM</a> (90.9), and urban adult contemporary <a href="/wiki/WRNB" title="WRNB">WRNB-FM</a> (100.3).<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Philadelphia is served by three non-commercial <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public radio</a> stations: WHYY-FM (<a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/WRTI" title="WRTI">WRTI-FM</a> (classical and jazz),<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/WXPN" title="WXPN">WXPN-FM</a> (adult alternative music).<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WTP_D03_AMP_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/WTP_D03_AMP_1.jpg/170px-WTP_D03_AMP_1.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/WTP_D03_AMP_1.jpg/255px-WTP_D03_AMP_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/WTP_D03_AMP_1.jpg/340px-WTP_D03_AMP_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WTP_D03_AMP_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Original <a href="/wiki/WCAU" title="WCAU">WCAU</a> studio at 1622 Chestnut Street</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 1930s, the experimental station <a href="/wiki/KYW-TV" title="KYW-TV">W3XE</a>, owned by <a href="/wiki/Philco" title="Philco">Philco</a>, became the first television station in Philadelphia. The station became <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>\'s first affiliate in 1939, and later became <a href="/wiki/KYW-TV" title="KYW-TV">KYW-TV</a> (currently a <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> affiliate). <a href="/wiki/WCAU" title="WCAU">WCAU-TV</a>, WFIL-TV, and <a href="/wiki/WHYY-TV" title="WHYY-TV">WHYY-TV</a> were all founded by the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-Media_288-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Media-288">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> In 1952, WFIL (renamed <a href="/wiki/WPVI-TV" title="WPVI-TV">WPVI</a>) premiered the television show <i>Bandstand</i>, which later became the nationally broadcast <i><a href="/wiki/American_Bandstand" title="American Bandstand">American Bandstand</a></i> hosted by <a href="/wiki/Dick_Clark" title="Dick Clark">Dick Clark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Each commercial network has an affiliate, and call letters have been replaced by corporate branding for promotional purposes: <a href="/wiki/KYW-TV" title="KYW-TV">CBS3</a>, <a href="/wiki/WPVI-TV" title="WPVI-TV">6ABC</a>, <a href="/wiki/WCAU" title="WCAU">NBC10</a>, <a href="/wiki/WPHL-TV" title="WPHL-TV">PHL17</a>, <a href="/wiki/WTXF-TV" title="WTXF-TV">Fox29</a>, <a href="/wiki/WPSG" title="WPSG">The CW Philly 57</a>, <a href="/wiki/WFPA-CD" title="WFPA-CD">UniM\xc3\xa1s Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/WWSI" title="WWSI">Telemundo62</a>, and <a href="/wiki/WUVP-DT" title="WUVP-DT">Univision65</a>. The region is served also by <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public broadcasting</a> stations <a href="/wiki/WPPT_(TV)" title="WPPT (TV)">WPPT-TV</a> (Philadelphia), <a href="/wiki/WHYY-TV" title="WHYY-TV">WHYY-TV</a> (Wilmington, Delaware and Philadelphia), <a href="/wiki/WLVT-TV" title="WLVT-TV">WLVT-TV</a> (Lehigh Valley), and <a href="/wiki/NJTV" title="NJTV">NJTV</a> (New Jersey).<sup id="cite_ref-TVstations_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TVstations-297">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philadelphia has <a href="/wiki/Owned-and-operated_station" title="Owned-and-operated station">owned-and-operated stations</a> for all five major English-language broadcast networks: <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/WCAU" title="WCAU">WCAU-TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/KYW-TV" title="KYW-TV">KYW-TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/WPVI-TV" title="WPVI-TV">WPVI-TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/WTXF-TV" title="WTXF-TV">WTXF-TV</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_CW" title="The CW">The CW</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/WPSG" title="WPSG">WPSG-TV</a>. The major Spanish-language networks are <a href="/wiki/Univision" title="Univision">Univision</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/WUVP-DT" title="WUVP-DT">WUVP-DT</a>, <a href="/wiki/UniM%C3%A1s" title="UniM\xc3\xa1s">UniM\xc3\xa1s</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/WFPA-CD" title="WFPA-CD">WFPA-CD</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telemundo" title="Telemundo">Telemundo</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/WWSI" title="WWSI">WWSI-TV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TVstations_297-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TVstations-297">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Philadelphia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the city is the nation\'s fourth-largest consumer in <a href="/wiki/Media_market" title="Media market">media market</a>, as ranked by the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Media_Research" title="Nielsen Media Research">Nielsen Media Research</a> firm, with nearly 2.9 million TV households.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:30th_Street_Station_Philadelphia_July_2016_002_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/30th_Street_Station_Philadelphia_July_2016_002_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-30th_Street_Station_Philadelphia_July_2016_002_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/30th_Street_Station_Philadelphia_July_2016_002_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-30th_Street_Station_Philadelphia_July_2016_002_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/30th_Street_Station_Philadelphia_July_2016_002_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-30th_Street_Station_Philadelphia_July_2016_002_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2292" data-file-height="1739" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:30th_Street_Station_Philadelphia_July_2016_002_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/30th_Street_Station" title="30th Street Station">30th Street Station</a>, seen in 2016, accommodates <a href="/wiki/SEPTA" title="SEPTA">SEPTA</a> Regional Rail and <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> service.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Philadelphia" title="Transportation in Philadelphia">Transportation in Philadelphia</a></div>\n<p>Philadelphia is served by the Southeastern Pennsylvania Transportation Authority (<a href="/wiki/SEPTA" title="SEPTA">SEPTA</a>) which operates buses, trains, <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> (subway and <a href="/wiki/Elevated_railway" title="Elevated railway">elevated trains</a>), <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trolleys</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trackless trolleys</a> (electric buses) throughout Philadelphia, the four Pennsylvania suburban counties of <a href="/wiki/Bucks_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Bucks County, Pennsylvania">Bucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chester_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Chester County, Pennsylvania">Chester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Delaware County, Pennsylvania">Delaware</a>, and <a
